  NADPH oxidase is an enzyme that produces ROS.

  Therefore, the enzyme that releases reactive oxygen metabolite in lysosomes is likely NADPH oxidase.

  Roots denuded for 6 years mean that the roots have been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibers are periodontal ligament fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  The cementum is a layer of hard, mineralized tissue that covers the root of the tooth.
  Dentin is the layer of the tooth beneath the enamel and cementum.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the body.
  Co-adaptation refers to the ability of the periodontal ligament fibers to adapt to changes in the tooth and surrounding bone.
  Therefore, since the roots have been denuded for 6 years, it is likely that the PDL fibers have been destroyed and the lateral sliding flap would show epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.
  The answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.

Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
  Malocclusion is a condition where the teeth are not properly aligned.
  Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population who have a specific condition at a particular time.
  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a specific condition in a population over a defined period of time.
  Morbidity refers to the occurrence of illness or disease in a population.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Malocclusion is a condition that is present in a population at a particular time, so prevalence rate is a better description of its occurrence.

  B: Pre-operational stage

Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease.
  Most oral hypoglycemic agents require renal dose modification in patients with chronic kidney disease.
  Linagliptin is a DPP-4 inhibitor that does not require renal dose adjustment.
  Repaglinide and Vildagliptin require dose adjustment in moderate to severe renal impairment.
  Glimepiride is contraindicated in severe renal impairment.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be Linagliptin.

  Repaglinide is a meglitinide and is contraindicated in patients with severe liver and/or kidney disease.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea and its metabolites are excreted by the kidneys. Therefore, it requires dose adjustment in patients with renal impairment.

Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is used for selecting samples from a large population.
  Simple random sampling is used for selecting samples from a small population.
  Stratified random sampling is used for selecting samples from a population that is divided into strata.
  Cluster sampling is used for selecting samples from a population that is divided into clusters.
  The question is asking about selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  This suggests that stratification may be necessary to ensure that the sample is representative.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is a method where every nth person is selected.
  Simple random sampling is a method where everyone has an equal chance of being selected.
  Stratified random sampling is a method where the population is divided into subgroups (strata) and then random sampling is done within each stratum.
  Cluster sampling is a method where the population is divided into clusters and then random sampling is done within each cluster.
  The method that is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results is Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
- Systematic random sampling is a type of probability sampling where every nth element is selected from a list or sequence.
- Simple random sampling is a type of probability sampling where each individual in the population has an equal chance of being selected.
- Stratified random sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into strata (subgroups) and individuals are selected from each stratum in proportion to their representation in the population.
- Cluster sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into clusters (groups) and a random sample of clusters is selected, and then all individuals within the selected clusters are included in the sample.
- The question is asking for a sampling method used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
- Stratified random sampling is the best choice because it allows for the selection of individuals from each stratum in proportion to their representation in the population.
- Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
